        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/968659.Little_House_on_the_Prairie" title="Hardcover 9780060264468" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4303446-megan?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4303446-megan?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4303446-megan?shelf=childrens-and-ya" class="actionLinkLite">childrens-and-ya</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer162751961">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13053109450442371480">I didn't like this one as much as the first book (<a title="Little House in the Big Woods (Little House, #1) by Laura Ingalls Wilder" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8337.Little_House_in_the_Big_Woods__Little_House___1_">Little House in the Big Woods</a>). Pa Ingalls kept pissing me off with all his stupid whims that kept putting the entire family in danger, and he never seemed too concerned when any of them came close to dying or getting severely hurt. "Oh, I just dropped a huge log on your leg, Ma? It's cool, just walk it off. You can drag your gimped-up leg behind you to get the water you'll need to make dinner tonight." "Oh snap, we all just survived malaria, woo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13053109450442371480">I didn't like this one as much as the first book (<a title="Little House in the Big Woods (Little House, #1) by Laura Ingalls Wilder" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8337.Little_House_in_the_Big_Woods__Little_House___1_">Little House in the Big Woods</a>). Pa Ingalls kept pissing me off with all his stupid whims that kept putting the entire family in danger, and he never seemed too concerned when any of them came close to dying or getting severely hurt. "Oh, I just dropped a huge log on your leg, Ma? It's cool, just walk it off. You can drag your gimped-up leg behind you to get the water you'll need to make dinner tonight." "Oh snap, we all just survived malaria, woo! Word around the campfire is that watermelons caused it? Screw that, I'm gonna go get one and eat it anyway - here, kids!" Those are the first two examples that spring to mind but there were several other instances. I don't know how Ma put up with all that and always kept her cool. So, overall, this one was pretty disappointing. Hopefully the next book gets better. Was the TV series based on just this book or the whole series?</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_14542335">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14542335" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/328247-samantha" class="left imgcol" title="Samantha"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1345151706p2/328247.jpg" alt="Samantha" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/14542335?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 04, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/328247-samantha" class="user" title="Samantha">Samantha</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/233633.Little_House_on_the_Prairie" title="Hardcover 9780060264451" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">8 to 14 year olds</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/328247-samantha?shelf=youth" class="actionLinkLite">youth</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer14542335">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12350710503311248035">The language of the book is very simple, seeing the prairie through the eyes of a young girl. The chapters are short and flow quickly, making this an excellent book for young readers just starting chapter books. The time period in which the book was written can be felt from the harsh, characterized, portrayal of American Indians, including the Osage tribe, rekindling the touchy phrase of General Sheridan’s remark declaring the only good Indian is a dead Indian.<br /><br />Though I enjoyed the illustrations</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12350710503311248035">The language of the book is very simple, seeing the prairie through the eyes of a young girl. The chapters are short and flow quickly, making this an excellent book for young readers just starting chapter books. The time period in which the book was written can be felt from the harsh, characterized, portrayal of American Indians, including the Osage tribe, rekindling the touchy phrase of General Sheridan’s remark declaring the only good Indian is a dead Indian.<br /><br />Though I enjoyed the illustrations by Garth Williams I had to push myself through this book. I feel I may have been over saturated with covered wagon tales in my own childhood as well as spoiled by my playing of “The Oregon Trail” computer game. The main adversary in the book was life and the elements themselves which were very subdued. I was also off put by Wilder’s description of American Indians as barbaric beggars or thieves. “They were tall, thin, fierce-looking men. Their skin was brownish-red. Their heads seemed to go up to a peak, and the peak was a tuft of hair that stood straight up and ended in feathers. Their eyes were black and still and glittering, like a snake’s eyes…Their faces were bold and fierce and terrible.” <br /><br />I understand that this book was introduced to many readers when they were young and has a special place in thier hearts. I feel the book is rather dated and almost dull.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12350710503311248035">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zxVpVkDaywdk/Hbw0bUrcODn7pyFsw6xo/vMey3mHCbrhQsNEKJe/89xxd8tgKOLAnbf+/uQZPSqixrNII3KUg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5300.Laura_Ingalls_Wilder">About Laura Ingalls Wilder</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/5300.Laura_Ingalls_Wilder"><img alt="5300" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1347574987p2/5300.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer7005788825245800752">Ingalls wrote a series of historical fiction books for children based on her childhood growing up in a pioneer family. She also wrote a regular newspaper column and kept a diary as an adult moving from South Dakota to Missouri, the latter of which has been published as a book.</span>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/5300.Laura_Ingalls_Wilder" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Laura Ingalls Wilder...</a>

        script.async = true;
        script.src = load[i];
        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]&gt;
</script>
